To compute the defining uses in parent\n   132→    /// bodies, we need the closure requirements of its nested bodies, but to check\n   133→    /// non-defining uses in nested bodies, we may rely on the defining uses in the\n   134→    /// parent.\n   135→    ///\n   136→    /// We handle this issue by applying closure requirements twice. In this case they get removed from\n   142→    /// `collect_region_constraints_results` and the final result gets put into\n   143→    /// `propagated_borrowck_results`.\n   144→    fn apply_closure_requirements_modulo_opaques(&mut self) {\n   145→        let mut closure_requirements_modulo_opaques = FxHashMap::default();\n   146→        // We need to `mem::take` both `self.collect_region_constraints_results` and\n   147→        // `input.deferred_closure_requirements` as we otherwise can't iterate over\n   148→        // them while mutably using the containing struct.\n   149→        let collect_region_constraints_results =\n   150→            mem::take(&mut self.collect_region_constraints_results);\n   151→        // We iterate over all bodies here, visiting nested bodies before their parent.\n   152→        for (def_id, mut input) in collect_region_constraints_results {\n   153→            // A body depends on opaque types if it either has any opaque type uses itself,\n   154→            // or it has a nested body which does.\n   155→            //\n   156→            // If the current body does not depend on any opaque types, we eagerly compute\n   157→            // its final result and write it into `self.propagated_borrowck_results`. This\n   158→            // avoids having to compute its closure requirements modulo regions, as they\n   159→            // are just the same as its final closure requirements.\n   160→            let mut depends_on_opaques = input.infcx.has_opaque_types_in_storage();\n   161→\n   162→            // Iterate over all nested bodies of `input`. If that nested body depends on\n   163→            // opaque types, we apply its closure requirements modulo opaques. Otherwise\n   164→            // we use the closure requirements from its final borrowck result.\n   165→            //\n   166→            // In case we've only applied the closure requirements modulo opaques, we have\n   167→            // to later apply its closure requirements considering opaques, so we put that\n   168→            // nested body back into `deferred_closure_requirements`.\n   169→            for (def_id, args, locations) in mem::take(&mut input.deferred_closure_requirements) {\n   170→                let closure_requirements = match self.propagated_borrowck_results.get(&def_id) {\n   171→                    None => {\n   172→                        depends_on_opaques = true;\n   173→                        input.deferred_closure_requirements.push((def_id, args, locations));\n   174→                        &closure_requirements_modulo_opaques[&def_id]\n   175→                    }\n   176→                    Some(result) => &result.closure_requirements,\n   177→                };\n   178→\n   179→                Self::apply_closure_requirements(\n   180→                    &mut input,\n   181→                    closure_requirements,\n   182→                    def_id,\n   183→                    args,\n   184→                    locations,\n   185→                );\n   186→            }\n        // we're able to use it when visiting its parent later in this function.\n   191→            //\n   192→            // If the current body does not depend on opaque types, we finish borrowck\n &closure_requirements_modulo_opaques[&def_id]\n                    }\n                    Some(result) => &result.closure_requirements,\n                };\n\n borrowck_check_region_constraints(self, input);\n                self.propagated_borrowck_results.insert(def_id, result);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_018tkArr182ZXbM526VvRLso","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→//! The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \"root\" of the\n     2→//! borrow forwards, iterating over \"similar\" projections in lockstep until\n     3→//! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\n     4→//! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\n     5→//!\n     6→//! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\n     7→//! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\n     8→//!\n     9→//! For example, if we are comparing these:\n    10→//! ```text\n    11→//! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\n    12→//! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\n    13→//! ```\n    14→//!\n    15→//! Then our steps are:\n    16→//! ```text\n    17→//!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\n    18→//!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\n    19→//!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\n    20→//!      *x1[2].y    |  *x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\n    21→//!     (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\n    22→//! ```\n    23→//!\n    24→//! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\n    25→//! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\n    26→//!\n    27→//! ```text\n    28→//! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\n    29→//! ACCESS:  x1[i].y\n    30→//! ```\n    31→//!\n    32→//! Then our steps are:\n    33→//! ```text\n    34→//!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\n    35→//!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\n    36→//!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\n    37→//! ```\n    38→//!\n    39→//! -- here we run out of access - the borrow can access a part of it. If this\n    40→//! is a full deep access, then we *know* the borrow conflicts with it. However,\n    41→//! if the access is shallow, then we can proceed:\n    42→//!\n    43→//! ```text\n    44→//!       x1[2].y    | (*x1[i].y)    -- a deref! the access can't get past this, so we\n    45→//!                                     are disjoint\n    46→//! ```\n    47→//!\n    48→//! Our invariant is, that at each step of the iteration:\n    49→//!  - If we didn't run out of access to match, our borrow and access are comparable\n    50→//!    and either equal or disjoint.\n    51→//!  - If we did run out of access, the borrow can access a part of it.\n    52→\n    53→use std::cmp::max;\n    54→use std::iter;\n    55→\n    56→use rustc_hir as hir;\n    57→use rustc_middle::bug;\n    58→use rustc_middle::mir::{\n    59→    Body, BorrowKind, FakeBorrowKind, MutBorrowKind, Place, PlaceElem, PlaceRef, ProjectionElem,\n    60→};\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \"root\" of the\n//! borrow forwards, iterating over \"similar\" projections in lockstep until\n//! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\n//! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\n//!\n//! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\n//! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\n//!\n//! For example, if we are comparing these:\n//! ```text\n//! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\n//! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\n//! ```\n//!\n//! Then our steps are:\n//! ```text\n//!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\n//!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\n//!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\n//!      *x1[2].y    |  *x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\n//!     (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\n//! ```\n//!\n//! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\n//! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\n//!\n//! ```text\n//! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\n//! ACCESS:  x1[i].y\n//! ```\n//!\n//! Then our steps are:\n//! ```text\n//!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\n//!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\n//!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\n//! ```\n//!\n//! -- here we run out of access - the borrow can access a part of it. If this\n//! is a full deep access, then we *know* the borrow conflicts with it. However,\n//! if the access is shallow, then we can proceed:\n//!\n//! ```text\n//!       x1[2].y    | (*x1[i].y)    -- a deref! the access can't get past this, so we\n//!                                     are disjoint\n//! ```\n//!\n//! Our invariant is, that at each step of the iteration:\n//!  - If we didn't run out of access to match, our borrow and access are comparable\n//!    and either equal or disjoint.\n//!  - If we did run out of access, the borrow can access a part of it.\n\nuse std::cmp::max;\nuse std::iter;\n\nuse rustc_hir as hir;\nuse rustc_middle::bug;\nuse rustc_middle::mir::{\n    Body, BorrowKind, FakeBorrowKind, MutBorrowKind, Place, PlaceElem, PlaceRef, ProjectionElem,\n};","numLines":60,"startLine":1,"totalLines":527}}}

Returns a set of (ty, location) pairs\n    24→/// that indicate which types must be live at which point in the CFG.\n    25→/// This vector is consumed by `constraint_generation`.\n    26→///\n    27→/// N.B., this computation requires normalization; therefore, it must be\n    28→/// performed before\n    29→pub(super) fn generate<'tcx>(\n    30→    typeck: &mut TypeChecker<'_, 'tcx>,\n    31→    location_map: &DenseLocationMap,\n    32→    move_data: &MoveData<'tcx>,\n    33→) {\n    34→    debug!(\"liveness::generate\");\n    35→\n    36→    let mut free_regions =    41→\n    42→    // NLLs can avoid computing some liveness data here because its constraints are\n    43→    // location-insensitive, but that doesn't work in polonius: locals whose type contains a region\n    44→    // that outlives a free region are not necessarily live everywhere in a flow-sensitive setting,\n    45→    // unlike NLLs.\n    46→    // We do record these regions in the polonius context, since they're used to differentiate\n    47→    // relevant and boring locals, which is a key distinction used later in diagnostics.\n    48→    if typeck.tcx().sess.opts.unstable_opts.polonius.is_next_enabled() {\n    49→        let (_, boring_locals) =\n    50→            compute_relevant_live_locals(typeck.tcx(), &free_regions, typeck.body);\n    51→        typeck.polonius_liveness.as_mut().unwrap().boring_nll_locals =\n    52→            boring_locals.into_iter().collect();\n    53→        free_regions = typeck.universal_regions.universal_regions_iter().collect();\n    54→    }\n    55→    let (relevant_live_locals, boring_locals) =\n    56→        compute_relevant_live_locals(typeck.tcx(), &free_regions, typeck.body);\n    57→\n    58→    trace::trace(typeck, location_map, move_data, relevant_live_locals, boring_locals);\n    59→\n    60→    // Mark regions that should be live where they appear within rvalues or within a call: like\n    61→    // args, regions, and types.\n    62→    record_regular_live_regions(\n    63→        typeck.tcx(),\n    64→        &mut typeck.constraints.liveness_constraints,\n    65→        &typeck.universal_regions,\n    66→        &mut typeck.polonius_liveness,\n    67→        typeck.body,\n    68→    );\n    69→}\n    70→\n    71→// The purpose of `compute_relevant_live_locals` is to define the subset of `Local`\n    72→// variables for which we need to do a liveness computation. We only need\n    73→// to compute whether a variable `X` is live if that variable contains\n    74→// some region `R` in its type where `R` is not known to outlive a free\n    75→// region (i.e., where `R` may be valid for just a subset of the fn body).\n    76→fn compute_relevant_live_locals<'tcx>(\n    77→    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n    78→    free_regions: &FxHashSet<RegionVid>,\n    79→    body: &Body<'tcx>,\n    80→) -> (Vec<Local>, Vec<Local>) {\n    81→    let (boring_locals, relevant_live_locals): (Vec<_>, Vec<_>) =\n    82→        body.local_decls.iter_enumerated().partition_map(|(local, local_decl)| {\n    83→            if tcx.all_free_regions_meet(&local_decl.ty, |r| free_regions.contains(&r.as_var())) {\n    84→                Either::Left(local)\n    85→            } else {\n    86→                Either::Right(local)\n    87→            }\n    88→        });\n    89→\n    90→    debug!(\"{} total variables\", body.local_decls.len());\n    91→    debug!(\"{} variables need liveness\", relevant_live_locals.len());\n    92→    debug!(\"{} regions outlive free regions\", free_regions.len());\n    93→\n    94→    (relevant_live_locals, boring_locals)\n    95→}\n    96→\n    97→/// Computes all regions that are (currently) known to outlive free\n    98→/// regions. For these regions, we do not need to compute\n    99→/// liveness, since the outlives constraints will ensure that they\n   100→/// are live over the whole fn body anyhow.\n   101→fn regions_that_outlive_free_regions<'tcx>(\n   102→    num_region_vars: usize,\n   103→    universal_regions: &UniversalRegions<'tcx>,\n   104→    constraint_set: &OutlivesConstraintSet<'tcx>,\n   105→) -> FxHashSet<RegionVid> {\n   106→    // Build a graph of the outlives constraints thus far. This is\n   107→    // a reverse graph, so for each constraint `R1: R2` we have an\n   108→    // edge `R2 -> R1`. Therefore, if we find all regions\n   109→    // reachable from each free region, we will have all the\n   110→    // regions that are forced to outlive some free region.\n   111→    let rev_constraint_graph = constraint_set.reverse_graph(num_region_vars);\n   112→    let fr_static = universal_regions.fr_static;\n   113→    let rev_region_graph = rev_constraint_graph.region_graph(constraint_set, fr_static);\n   114→\n   115→    // Stack for the depth-first search. Start out with all the free regions.\n   116→    let mut stack: Vec<_> = universal_regions.universal_regions_iter().collect();\n   117→\n   118→    // Set of all free regions, plus anything that outlives them.
